    (function () {
        if ( typeof window.CustomEvent === "function" ) return false;
        function CustomEvent ( event, params ) {
            params = params || { bubbles: false, cancelable: false, detail: null };
            var evt = document.createEvent( 'CustomEvent' );
            evt.initCustomEvent( event, params.bubbles, params.cancelable, params.detail );
            return evt;
        }

        CustomEvent.prototype = window.Event.prototype;

        window.CustomEvent = CustomEvent;
    })();
</script>

    <meta name="journal_id" content="41438"/>

    <meta name="dc.title" content="A high-quality genome provides insights into the new taxonomic status and genomic characteristics of Cladopus chinensis (Podostemaceae)"/>

    <meta name="dc.source" content="Horticulture Research 2020 7:1"/>

    <meta name="dc.format" content="text/html"/>

    <meta name="dc.publisher" content="Nature Publishing Group"/>

    <meta name="dc.date" content="2020-04-01"/>

    <meta name="dc.type" content="OriginalPaper"/>

    <meta name="dc.language" content="En"/>

    <meta name="dc.copyright" content="2020 The Author(s)"/>

    <meta name="dc.rightsAgent" content="journalpermissions@springernature.com"/>

    <meta name="dc.description" content="The Podostemaceae are ecologically and morphologically unusual aquatic angiosperms that survive only in rivers with pristine hydrology and high water quality and are at a relatively high risk of extinction. The taxonomic status of Podostemaceae has always been controversial. Here, we report the first high-quality genome assembly for Cladopus chinensis of Podostemaceae, obtained by incorporating Hi-C, Illumina and PacBio sequencing. We generated an 827.92&#8201;Mb genome with a contig N50 of 1.42&#8201;Mb and 27,370 annotated protein-coding genes. The assembled genome size was close to the estimated size, and 659.42&#8201;Mb of the assembly was assigned to 29 superscaffolds (scaffold N50 21.22&#8201;Mb). A total of 59.20% repetitive sequences were identified, among which long terminal repeats (LTRs) were the most abundant class (28.97% of the genome). Genome evolution analysis suggested that the divergence time of Cladopus chinensis (106 Mya) was earlier than that of Malpighiales (82 Mya) and that this taxon diverged into an independent branch of Podestemales. A recent whole-genome duplication (WGD) event occurred 4.43 million years ago. Comparative genomic analysis revealed that the expansion and contraction of oxidative phosphorylation, photosynthesis and isoflavonoid metabolism genes in Cladopus chinensis are probably related to the genomic characteristics of this growing submerged species. Transcriptome analysis revealed that upregulated genes in the shoot group compared to the root group were enriched in the NAC gene family and transcription factors associated with shoot development and defense responses, including WUSCHEL (WUS), ASYMMETRIC LEAVES (ASL), SHOOT MERISTEMLESS (STM), NAC2, NAC8, NAC29, NAC47, NAC73, NAC83 and NAC102. These findings provide new insights into the genomic diversity of unusual aquatic angiosperms and serve as a valuable reference for the taxonomic status and unusual shoot apical meristem of Podostemaceae."/>

    <meta name="description" content="The Podostemaceae are ecologically and morphologically unusual aquatic angiosperms that survive only in rivers with pristine hydrology and high water quality and are at a relatively high risk of extinction. The taxonomic status of Podostemaceae has always been controversial. Here, we report the first high-quality genome assembly for Cladopus chinensis of Podostemaceae, obtained by incorporating Hi-C, Illumina and PacBio sequencing. We generated an 827.92&#8201;Mb genome with a contig N50 of 1.42&#8201;Mb and 27,370 annotated protein-coding genes. The assembled genome size was close to the estimated size, and 659.42&#8201;Mb of the assembly was assigned to 29 superscaffolds (scaffold N50 21.22&#8201;Mb). A total of 59.20% repetitive sequences were identified, among which long terminal repeats (LTRs) were the most abundant class (28.97% of the genome). Genome evolution analysis suggested that the divergence time of Cladopus chinensis (106 Mya) was earlier than that of Malpighiales (82 Mya) and that this taxon diverged into an independent branch of Podestemales. A recent whole-genome duplication (WGD) event occurred 4.43 million years ago. Comparative genomic analysis revealed that the expansion and contraction of oxidative phosphorylation, photosynthesis and isoflavonoid metabolism genes in Cladopus chinensis are probably related to the genomic characteristics of this growing submerged species. Transcriptome analysis revealed that upregulated genes in the shoot group compared to the root group were enriched in the NAC gene family and transcription factors associated with shoot development and defense responses, including WUSCHEL (WUS), ASYMMETRIC LEAVES (ASL), SHOOT MERISTEMLESS (STM), NAC2, NAC8, NAC29, NAC47, NAC73, NAC83 and NAC102. These findings provide new insights into the genomic diversity of unusual aquatic angiosperms and serve as a valuable reference for the taxonomic status and unusual shoot apical meristem of Podostemaceae."/>

2478, grid.411503.2, Public Service Platform for Industrialization Development Technology of Marine Biological Medicine and Products of the State Oceanic Administration, Fujian Key Laboratory of Special Marine Bioresource Sustainable Utilization, Key Laboratory of Developmental and Neural Biology, College of Life Sciences, Fujian Normal University, Fuzhou, China" /></span></sup>, </li><li             <div class="c-article-body">
                <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><p>The Podostemaceae are ecologically and morphologically unusual aquatic angiosperms that survive only in rivers with pristine hydrology and high water quality and are at a relatively high risk of extinction. The taxonomic status of Podostemaceae has always been controversial. Here, we report the first high-quality genome assembly for <i>Cladopus chinensis</i> of Podostemaceae, obtained by incorporating Hi-C, Illumina and PacBio sequencing. We generated an 827.92âMb genome with a contig N50 of 1.42âMb and 27,370 annotated protein-coding genes. The assembled genome size was close to the estimated size, and 659.42âMb of the assembly was assigned to 29 superscaffolds (scaffold N50 21.22âMb). A total of 59.20% repetitive sequences were identified, among which long terminal repeats (LTRs) were the most abundant class (28.97% of the genome). Genome evolution analysis suggested that the divergence time of <i>Cladopus chinensis</i> (106 Mya) was earlier than that of Malpighiales (82 Mya) and that this taxon diverged into an independent branch of Podestemales. A recent whole-genome duplication (WGD) event occurred 4.43 million years ago. Comparative genomic analysis revealed that the expansion and contraction of oxidative phosphorylation, photosynthesis and isoflavonoid metabolism genes in <i>Cladopus chinensis</i> are probably related to the genomic characteristics of this growing submerged species. Transcriptome analysis revealed that upregulated genes in the shoot group compared to the root group were enriched in the NAC gene family and transcription factors associated with shoot development and defense responses, including WUSCHEL (WUS), ASYMMETRIC LEAVES (ASL), SHOOT MERISTEMLESS (STM), NAC2, NAC8, NAC29, NAC47, NAC73, NAC83 and NAC102. These findings provide new insights into the genomic diversity of unusual aquatic angiosperms and serve as a valuable reference for the taxonomic status and unusual shoot apical meristem of Podostemaceae.</p></div></div></section>

                    <section aria-labelledby="Sec1" data-title="Introduction"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1">Introduction</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content"><p>Podostemaceae are freshwater hydrophytes whose center of diversity is the Neotropics. In the Amazon, these species form subaquatic meadows producing autochthonous carbon, which serve as a source of food for the associated fauna<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Vinicius, N. L. et al. High importance of autochthonous basal food source for the food web of a brazilian tropical stream regardless of shading. Int. Rev. Hydrobiol. 101, 132â142 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d28073e550">1</a></sup>. The Amazon is the richest region of Podostemaceae occurrence<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Sobral-Leite, M. et al. Anthecology and reproductive system of mourera fluviatilis (podostemaceae): pollination by bees and xenogamy in a predominantly anemophilous and autogamous family? Aquat. Bot. 95, 0â87 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d28073e554">2</a></sup>. These plants require rivers with pristine hydrology and good water quality, which are very important characteristics for their productivity and for maintaining the associated fauna, and their destruction can lead to ecological and economic losses as well as the loss of cultural and hedonic value<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Ram, H. Y. M. &amp; Sehgal, A. In vitro studies on developmental morphology of indian podostemaceae. Aquat. Bot. 57, 0â132 (1997)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d28073e558">3</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Cruden &amp; Robert, W. Pollen-ovule ratios: a conservative indicator of breeding systems in flowering plants. Evolution 31, 32â46 (1977)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d28073e561">4</a></sup>.</p><p>Podostemaceae is a morphologically and esthetically aquatic angiosperm family distributed in the rivers of tropical, subtropical and temperate regions<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Koi, S. &amp; Kato, M. Paracladopus chanthaburiensis, a new species of Podostemaceae from thailand, with notes on its morphology, phylogeny and distribution. Taxon 57, 201â210 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d28073e568">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Katayama, N., Kato, M. &amp; Imaichi, R. Habitat specificity enhances genetic differentiation in two species of aquatic Podostemaceae in Japan. Am. J. Bot. 103, 317â324 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d28073e571">6</a></sup>. Angiosperms normally exhibit a common system of gravitropism (the growth movement of organs in response to gravity). The roots grow downward into the soil, and the shoots upward in this gravitropism system. The plant meristems, including the root apical meristem (RAM) and shoot apical meristem (SAM), are unique structures of undifferentiated pluripotent stem cells<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Koi, S., Imaichi, R. &amp; Kato, M. Endogenous leaf initiation in the apicalâmeristemless shoot ofcladopus queenslandicus (Podostemaceae) and implications for evolution of shoot morphology. Int. J. Plant. Sci. 166, 199â206 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d28073e575">7</a></sup>. However, Podostemaceae, Streptocarpus and Lemnaceae exhibit unusual modifications of the SAM that may reflect adaptation to new habitats and can subsequently diversify in the evolution of plants<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Katayama, N., Koi, S. &amp; Kato, M. Expression of shoot meristemless, wuschel, and asymmetric leaves1 homologs in the shoots of Podostemaceae: implications for the evolution of novel shoot organogenesis. Plant Cell 22, 2131â2140 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d28073e579">8</a></sup>.</p><p>Several studies have focused on the establishment of the SAM, including the auxin-related gene activities, transcription factors and morphological characteristics involved<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Shani, E., Yanai, O. &amp; Ori, N. The role of hormones in shoot apical meristem function. Curr. Opin. Plant. Biol. 9, 484â489 (2006)." href="#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d28073e586">9</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Luo, L. et al. A molecular framework for auxin-controlled homeostasis of shoot stem cells in Arabidopsis. Mol. Plant 7, 899â913 (2018)." href="#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d28073e586_1">10</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Landau, U. et al. The erecta, clavata and class iii hd-zip pathways display synergistic interactions in regulating floral meristem activities. PLoS ONE 10, e0125408 (2015)." href="#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d28073e586_2">11</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Cole, M. Nuclear import of the transcription factor shoot meristemless depends on heterodimerization with blh proteins expressed in discrete sub-domains of the shoot apical meristem of arabidopsis thaliana. Nucleic Acids Res. 34, 1281â1292 (2006)." href="#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d28073e586_3">12</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Hamada, S. et al. Mutations in the WUSCHEL gene of Arabidopsis thaliana result in the development of shoots without juvenile leaves. Plant J. 24, 91â101 (2000)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d28073e589">13</a></sup>. A low auxin level contributes to the initial establishment of the apical-basal axis that extends to form the apical meristems of the shoots<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Shani, E., Yanai, O. &amp; Ori, N. The role of hormones in shoot apical meristem function. Curr. Opin. Plant. Biol. 9, 484â489 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d28073e593">9</a></sup>. The monopteros (MP) gene encodes an auxin response factor whose activity as a transcriptional activator facilitates auxin flow by promoting vascular development. MP expression is relatively weak in auxin-deficient conditions<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Luo, L. et al. A molecular framework for auxin-controlled homeostasis of shoot stem cells in Arabidopsis. Mol. Plant 7, 899â913 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d28073e597">10</a></sup>. WUSCHEL (WUS) is a homeodomain transcription factor whose expression establishes a de novo stem cell population<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Landau, U. et al. The erecta, clavata and class iii hd-zip pathways display synergistic interactions in regulating floral meristem activities. PLoS ONE 10, e0125408 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d28073e601">11</a></sup>. SHOOT MERISTEMLESS (STM) encodes a MEINOX/three-amino acid loop extension (TALE)-HD-type transcription factor required for the initiation and maintenance of the SAM<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Cole, M. Nuclear import of the transcription factor shoot meristemless depends on heterodimerization with blh proteins expressed in discrete sub-domains of the shoot apical meristem of arabidopsis thaliana. Nucleic Acids Res. 34, 1281â1292 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d28073e605">12</a></sup>. Hamada et al. reported that mutations of the WUS gene in <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i> halt the entire process of SAM formation and result in no production of juvenile leaves<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Hamada, S. et al. Mutations in the WUSCHEL gene of Arabidopsis thaliana result in the development of shoots without juvenile leaves. Plant J. 24, 91â101 (2000)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d28073e613">13</a></sup>. Based on these studies, the SAM is deemed vital for the vegetative growth of the stem and produces determinate lateral leaves with shoot branches at their axils, which is associated with the expression of key regulatory genes in the evolution of plant organization.</p><p>Podostemaceae species grow submerged on rock surfaces in rapids and waterfalls during the rainy season and bear flowers above the water during the dry season, when the water level decreases<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Rutishauser, R. Evolution of unusual morphologies in lentibulariaceae (bladderworts and allies) and podostemaceae (river-weeds): a pictorial report at the interface of developmental biology and morphological diversification. Ann. Bot. 117, 811â832 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d28073e620">14</a></sup>. Studies involving large amounts of data have mainly been concentrated in certain geographical regions and focused on the molecular phylogenetic analysis of Podostemaceae among other angiosperms, including the evaluation of the phylogeny, classification, and biogeography of Podostemaceae as a whole<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Koi, S. et al. Molecular phylogenetic analysis of Podostemaceae: implications for taxonomy of major groups. Bot. J. Lin. Soc. 169, 461â492 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d28073e624">15</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Kato, M., Wong, M. C. K., Lo, J. P. &amp; Satoshi, K. A cladopus species (Podostemaceae) rediscovered from Hong Kong. Acta Phytotax. 68, 17â22 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d28073e627">16</a></sup>. However, little is known about the evolution of the distinct shoot and root systems of Podostemaceae. Katayama et al. examined the expression patterns of the STM, WUS and asymmetric leaves (ASL) genes related to shoot development in Tristichoideae and Podostemoideae<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Katayama, N., Koi, S. &amp; Kato, M. Expression of shoot meristemless, wuschel, and asymmetric leaves1 homologs in the shoots of Podostemaceae: implications for the evolution of novel shoot organogenesis. Plant Cell 22, 2131â2140 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d28073e631">8</a></sup>. The subfamily Tristichoideae shows typical shoot organogenesis with a tunica-corpus SAM that produced leaves, but Podostemoideae is devoid of SAM, and new leaves in these plants develop below the older leaves without a SAM structure. Katayama et al. found that the leaves or bracts of Podostemoideae were involved in SAM initiation and maintenance and differentiated into single apical leaves or bracts, resulting in the evolution of mixed shoot-leaf organs in Podostemaceae according to the analysis of phylogenetic and expression patterns<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Katayama, N., Koi, S. &amp; Kato, M. Expression of shoot meristemless, wuschel, and asymmetric leaves1 homologs in the shoots of Podostemaceae: implications for the evolution of novel shoot organogenesis. Plant Cell 22, 2131â2140 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d28073e635">8</a></sup>. However, questions remain regarding how the unusual modification of the SAM arose during the evolution of Podostemaceae and what key regulatory genes are involved in the evolution of adaptation to the environment. The reasons for these phenomena are not clear. Furthermore, genomic information for Podostemaceae species has not been previously reported.</p><p><i>Cladopus chinensis</i> (<i>C. chinensis</i>) is a species of the genus <i>Cladopus</i> that exhibits flattened roots creeping on rock surfaces, and leaves and flowers are produced from the roots (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#Fig1">1</a>). <i>C. chinensis</i> can be used as an excellent material for studying the evolution of angiosperm morphology due to its extraordinary aerial shoots and underground root system<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Chao, H. C. Teratological variations of stamen in Lawiella chinensis Chao (Podostemonaceae) in relation to the taxonomic position of the genus. J. Univ. Chin. Aca. Sci. 1, 343â359 (1951)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d28073e657">17</a></sup>. Because of the limited genomic information available, an in-depth investigation of the genetic basis of <i>C. chinensis</i> is still lacking.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-1" data-title="Cladopus chinensis."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 1: <i>Cladopus chinensis</i>.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5/figures/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41438-020-0269-5/MediaObjects/41438_2020_269_Fig1_HTML.png?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-1-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41438-020-0269-5/MediaObjects/41438_2020_269_Fig1_HTML.png" alt="figure1" loading="lazy" width="685" height="465" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-1-desc"><p><b>a</b> Flowering plants in the habitat of the species. <b>b</b> Roots. <b>c</b> Leaves on sterile stems. <b>d</b> Flowering plants. <b>e</b> Flowering shoots (an-anther; ov-ovary; st-style). Barâ=â3âmm</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5/figures/1" data-track-dest="link:Figure1 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>In this study, to systematically understand the evolution of organogenesis in <i>C. chinensis</i>, we performed third-generation sequencing (TGS) on the PacBio SEQUEL platform and Hi-C technology to generate a high-quality genome assembly and annotation of <i>C. chinensis</i>. We also performed transcriptome sequencing to identify the genes that are involved in the diversity of SAM establishment. These results provide insight into the evolutionary model underlying shoot novelty in Podostemaceae.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec2" data-title="Results"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec2">Results</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec2-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec3">Genome sequencing and quality assembly</h3><p>We estimated a genome size of 820âMb for <i>C. chinensis</i>, with heterozygosity of 0.73% and a repeat content of 51.0% (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#MOESM2">S1</a>). A total of 95.36âGb of PacBio long reads (~105X coverage of the genome) and 106.2âGb of Illumina clean reads (~118X coverage of the genome) were generated, resulting in approximately 224.2-fold coverage of the <i>C. chinensis</i> genome (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#Tab1">1</a>). The total size of all reads assembled from the <i>C. chinensis</i> genome was 827.92âMb, consisting of 5629 contigs. The contig N50 was 1.42âMb, and the longest contig was 8.89âMb (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#Fig2">2</a> and Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#Tab2">2</a>). The genome size was close to the results based on flow cytometry (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#MOESM2">S2</a>) and genome surveys (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#MOESM2">S1</a>). The assembly quality was assessed through BUSCO analysis and the alignment of Illumina short reads to the genome. The NGS short reads from the Illumina sequencing platform were mapped to the contigs by using Bowtie2 software, and approximately 99.78% of the Illumina resequencing reads were mapped to the assembly (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#MOESM5">S1</a>). BUSCO analysis revealed that the assembly completeness was 90.7% in the <i>C. chinensis</i> genome (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#MOESM5">S2</a>). Using the contact matrix and the agglomerative hierarchical clustering method in LACHESIS<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Langmead, B. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. Fast gapped-read alignment with Bowtie 2. Nat. Methods 9, 357â359 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d28073e750">18</a></sup>, the 538 contigs were successfully clustered into 29 superscaffolds (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#Fig3">3</a>; Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#MOESM5">S3</a>). The scaffold N50 reached 1.42 and 21.22âMb (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#Tab2">2</a>), providing the first high-quality genome assembly for <i>C. chinensis</i>. Moreover, a total of 836 syntenic blocks were detected in the <i>C. chinensis</i> genome, which involved 15,410 genes. Synteny analysis of the 29 superscaffolds of <i>C. chinensis</i> confirmed that superscaffold no. 4 shared the most syntenic blocks with superscaffold no. 6 (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#Fig2">2</a>).</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-1"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab1" data-test="table-caption">Table 1 Sequencing data used for <i>C. chinensis</i> genome construction</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" <i>C. chinensis</i> genome</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-3" data-title="C. chinensis genome-wide all-by-all Hi-C interaction heat map."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig3" class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41438-020-0269-5/MediaObjects/41438_2020_269_Fig3_HTML.png?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-3-desc" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-3-desc"><p>The map shows high-resolution individual superscaffolds, which were scaffolded and assembled independently</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5/figures/3" data-track-dest="link:Figure3 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4">Gene prediction and functional annotation</h3><p>A combination of reference plant protein homology support, transcriptome data, and <i>ab initio</i> gene prediction was used to generate all gene models. All gene models were merged, and redundancy was removed with MAKER, leading to a total of 27,370 protein-coding genes. The average transcript length was 1465âbp, and the average CDS length was 868âbp (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#Tab3">3</a>). We functionally annotated 22,564, 14,193, 22,564 and 11,950 genes to the eggNOG, GO, COG and KEGG databases, respectively, leading to 23,163 (84.63% of the total) genes showing at least one hit to the public databases (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#Tab3">3</a>). In total, 2156 transcription factors were identified in the <i>C. chinensis</i> genome, and these genes were classified into 28 families, including 705 protein kinase family, 459 PPR, 155 MYB and 123 bHLH superfamily proteins (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#MOESM5">S4</a>).</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-3"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab3" data-test="table-caption">Table 3 Annotation statistics for the <i>C. chinensis</i> genome</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5/tables/3"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec5">Annotation of noncoding RNAs (ncRNAs)</h3><p>We identified snRNA, miRNA and rRNA genes in the <i>C. chinensis</i> genome from the Rfam database using BLASTN software (E-value â¤ 1e-5), and we used tRNAscan-SE and RNAmmer to predict tRNAs and rRNAs, resulting in a <i>C. chinensis</i> genome with 79 miRNAs, 1997 tRNAs, 397 rRNAs, 116 sRNAs, and 128 snRNAs (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#MOESM5">S5</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec6">Repeat element (TE) annotation and burst analysis</h3><p>The <i>C. chinensis</i> genome contained 490.13âMb of repetitive sequences, accounting for 59.20% of the genome (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#MOESM5">S6</a>). Long terminal repeat (LTR) retrotransposons accounted for 28.97% of the genome, with 22.30% Ty1/copia and 0.72% Ty3/gypsy sequences. Kimura distance analysis indicated an LTR burst (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#MOESM2">S3</a>) involving the Ty1/copia and Ty3/gypsy superfamilies. Tandem Repeats Finder identified over 50,071 tandem repeats, accounting for 7.40% of the <i>C. chinensis</i> genome (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#MOESM5">S6</a>). Telomeric and centromeric repeats were identified by searching the ends of contigs, and 8 telomeric repeat sequences and 572 centromeric repeat sequences were identified (Tables <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#MOESM5">S7</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#MOESM6">S8</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec7">Evolution of the <i>C. chinensis</i> genome</h3><p>We collected the genome sequences of representative plant species and performed comparative genomic analysis with <i>C. chinensis</i> to reveal the genome evolution and divergence time of <i>C. chinensis</i>. The results suggested that gene family contractions outnumbered expansions in <i>C. chinensis</i>, <i>R. communis</i>, <i>O. sativa</i>, <i>P. alba</i>, <i>B. oleracea</i>, <i>B. rapa</i>, <i>J. curcas</i>, <i>M. esculenta</i>, <i>A. thaliana</i>, <i>C. pepo</i> and <i>F. vesca</i>, in contrast to the other seven species (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#Fig4">4a</a>). The results support the view that Malpighiales and Rosales share a common Rosidae ancestor, which is the basal taxon of dicotyledons. The phylogenetic tree showed that <i>C. chinensis</i> phylogenetically diverged into an independent branch approximately 106 million years ago (Mya), without clustering into Malpighiales after the divergence of the <i>A. thaliana</i> (Brassicales) lineage 108 Mya. The data further confirmed that the divergence time of <i>C. chinensis</i> (106 Mya) was earlier than those of Malpighiales (82 Mya) and Rosales (102 Mya) and later than that of Brassicales (108 Mya). We also found that the internal branches separating Brassicales, Podestemales, Rosales, and Malpighiales were very short, as shown in Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#Fig4">4a</a>, suggesting the rapid diversification of these major clades. To obtain a highly reliable phylogenetic tree, we identified 91 single-copy homologous genes and performed coalescent analysis with RAxML and ASTRAL to estimate the species tree from gene trees. This result showed that <i>C. chinensis</i> phylogenetically clusters into Malpighiales, which is consistent with the results from NCBI Taxonomy (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#Fig4">4b</a>). On the basis of the number of transversions at four-fold degenerate sites, we calculated an age distribution for all duplicate gene pairs. Using 8,074 paralogous gene pairs of similar ages and excluding tandem or local duplications, a large peak centered on a synonymous substitution rate (<i>K</i><sub>s</sub>) of approximately 0.14 was observed in the <i>C. chinensis</i> genome (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5#Fig5">5</a>), indicating only one recent whole-genome duplication (WGD) event and one ancient WGD that occurred 4.43 million years ago.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-4" data-title="Phylogenetic tree and evolution analysis of C. chinensis."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig4" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 4: Phylogenetic tree and evolution analysis of <i>C. chinensis</i>.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5/figures/4" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41438-020-0269-5/MediaObjects/41438_2020_269_Fig4_HTML.png?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-4-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41438-020-0269-5/MediaObjects/41438_2020_269_Fig4_HTML.png" alt="figure4" loading="lazy" width="685" height="957" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-4-desc"><p><b>a</b> Phylogenetic tree showing the number of gene families displaying expansion (green) and contraction (red) among 18 plant species. The pie charts show the proportions of expanded (green), contracted (red) and conserved (blue) gene family among all gene families. The estimated divergence time (million years ago) is displayed below the phylogenetic tree in black. *The time of the occurrence of a recent whole-genome duplication (WGD) event in <i>C. chinensis</i>. MRCA, most recent common ancestor. <b>b</b> The species tree of 18 species inferred from the complete dataset of single-copy homologous gene using concatenation (RAxML) and gene-tree-based coalescent (ASTRAL) methods</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view 5</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41438-020-0269-5/figures/5" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp"
